<Author>AmKayD
<Content>Great Location, Friendly staff, Excellent Breakfast..... Stayed in this hotel from 24 dec 2008 for 3 nights. reservation was done through travelocity for US$156.34 per night including free breakfast for 2. during checkin, requested to have the room in the south tower but was told that additional S$50 for the upgrade. rejected it and was put on the 19th floor in the north tower. this is my first time staying in fairmont. the room had a king size bed, a balcony, bathtub, minibar full of beverages, a nice selection of tv channels. the room looks a bit old due to the wooden furnished. you can double confirm this when you checkout the wooden bathroom door. but besides this, the accessories in the room are top notch. you do not need to bring toiletries at all. they have shampoo, conditioner, moisturizer, dental kit, sewing kit, mouth wash, hair dryer, iron + ironing board, umbrella, bathroom slippers and the list goes... The TV is a flat screen CRT which is ok and nothing fancy. feather liked pillows is nice and soft. there are also some magazines to read. the room had a magnificent view facing towards the Singapore Plaza direction. the room gets cleaned up twice a day. In the morning and late afternoon which is a plus. the morning breakfast can be taken either at the 8th floor near to the swimming pool or at 2nd floor in the plaza market restaurant. the food serve at the swimming is more limited. i feel like it targets more for the western tourist since it lacks of the eastern cuisine but it is enough of you are a light eater. pasteries, cereals, buns, juices, fruits etc. plaza market restaurant however has a more variety of food. they have the fruit juice station where you can request to have your own fruit mixed! u also get to taste some of the eastern cuisine like curry chicken, roti prata, sambal, congee(porridge), soup. From my observation, most of the staff working here are from the mainland china although English is well understood and conversed. Overall, the service was excellent and the hotel was clean.

<Content>World of Difference: North Tower vs South Tower Rooms The last I wrote a review on Fairmont Hotel, was on Dec 6 2007, and rated it excellent. This year, on Dec 7 2008, I booked into the hotel again. This time, I stayed at the North Tower room, 1419 on Dec 7 2008. The room faces the pool. I finally figured out the vast difference in the reviews for Fairmont Singapore. There is a GREAT difference North Tower (Fairmont Rooms) vs South Tower (Deluxe Rooms).North Tower rooms are definitely shabby and trapped in time. I agree with some of the reviews in this website. Definitely not worth paying for. My brother  his family checked into the South Tower Room. It's a great positive contrast. Refer to my review on Dec 6 2007.The hotel shares the reception and the check-in time is EXTREMELY slow. Service staff is trying their best but overall service is slow. Guests could not be checked-in on time. I waited 2 hours from check-in time (2pm) and finally checked in at about 4pm. My brother could not check-in till 6pm. Service personnel tried to make it up by upgrading him to the club floor. What really puzzles me is that the long lead-time for check-in is consistent year-in year-out.

<Author>albertst
<Content>wonderful city, wonderful hotel We chose the Fairmont for a 10 day holiday stay because of its location and a good price for a 5 star hotel. (and after reading reviews on Trip Advisor) It didn't disapoint in any way. We previously stayed at the Sheraton Towers 4 years ago and enjoyed that, but wanted a more central location for 10 days. It was a wonderful experience, we felt so relaxed after our stay in SIngapore and that was certainly due to the Fairmont. We will definetly return next year for another holiday in this wonderful city. Many friends had said 10 days was a long time in SIngapore, but we still haven't been to the zoo, Changi or Sentosa, so there is plenty to do there!Our room was on the 21st floor (quick lifts) in the South Tower. Very comfortable and quite spacious with a view on the pool side looking out towards the Padang. The Raffles City Shopping Mall attached is lovely, with a sensational Japanese restaurant bazzar downstairs.The turndown service was great, lovely to come back each night to tidy room, soft lights and music and fresh towels. The bathroom was good, large with a goood sized bath, and a good shower that did splash a bit onto the rest of the floor. The airconditioner was silent and easily adjustable from the bedside console, as were the curtains and lights. Our room came with breakfast included and we alternated between the more traditional restaurant and the poolside buffet, service was personable and very responsive. We felt very well cared for. The buffets were wonderful, fresh tropical fruit juices individually prepared, cooked western breakfast on demand and Chinese and Malay fare with a wonderful array of pastries, the fresh fruits were outstanding. Breakfast on til 11 am as well helped jetlagged guests from Australia!The Fairmont staff were always welcoming and responsive. We had an extended checkout until 4 on the day we were leaving, and the offer of using the courtesy lounge by one of the staff whilst we were sitting in the foyer with our suitcases waiting for a taxi.Cleaning staff were always evident, and housekeeping responsive to our requests for cleaning whilst we were at breakfast. Sheets crisp and changed daily, (only on the last day of 10 days was a card left to say if we didn't need sheets changed to leave card on the bed, sure more water could've been saved!)My husband swam every afternoon in the circular pool on the 8th floor, never too crowded and for some reason a pleasant breeze blowing!Position is wondeful, CityHall MRT is at Raffles City Shopping Mall which is attached to the Fairmont. We walked every day, walking distance to the National Museum, History Museum, Peranakan Museum all highly reccommended. Easy MRT to Chinatown, Little India, Arab Quarter, Orchard Rd, Newton Food Markets, and on and on. Across the street is Raffles with a nice bakery, and good range of restaurants and bars. As you can see we loved the city and the hotel experience was a great one, perhaps the South Tower made the difference for us to the previous post, but thanks to TRipAdvisor we had read previously that the South Tower was the way to go. We will return.

<Author>RampantScot
<Content>Like stepping back to a shabby 1980s Just checked into Fairmont, Singapore (used to be Raffles Plaza...I think!) and not impressed. Been to Singapore many, many times and this was first visit to this hotel.Booked corporate rate of SGD305 plus local taxes per night through company (preferred hotel) but not worth it. Check in was fine, efficient and friendly. Great location but really shabby decor and very, very dated.Shocked to see graffiti on one of the doors in the hall way on the way to the room. Not typical for Singapore.Room on 7th floor is large, corner room but looks like a scene from a 1980's Dynasty show, all I need is my shoulder pads to really fit in. Dated furniture, dirty marked walls, wall paper is that material like stuff....like wool stuck to wall paper. Lots of gold coloured metal lamps, dated and battered furniture. Air conditioning has no adjustable temperature setting that I can find, still quite hot and humid, not good in Singapore.No wifi and cable link costs SGD28 plus tax per 24 hours.......even though I just needed an hour for work e-mails. It鈥檚 SGD28 for 24 hours minimum!Booked for 5 days but checking out tomorrow and moving to one of my regular hotels down the street for same price or less.If you get this room for SGD200ish, it's OK. If you are used to decent Singapore hotels, stick to Conrad, Pan Pacific or Mandarin Oriental. I could get the same rate or cheaper and they are more comfortable, modern and better maintained.This booking taught me to stick with my tried and tested favourites......and to check Trip Advisory before I book!Photos to follow!

<Author>Turkeyjay
<Content>Exemplary The hotel is approximately a 20-minute drive from Changi airport. The airport shuttle bus costs SD$9 per adult, taxi cost ~SD$14. It is conveniently located next to City Hall MRT station and the Raffles City shopping centre. It is within walking distance (through the airconditioned malls) to the Singapore Flyer. Check-in time is 2pm, but we were given a room straight away even though we arrived at 9am. Check-out time is 12 noon, but we were also allowed a late check-out of 3pm at no additional cost.We stayed in a Raffles Inc Club Room, which we found was excellent value for money. The room was large and included a balcony and impressive electronic day and night curtains. It was immaculately clean, comfortably and stylishly appointed. There was a very impressive Lavazza coffee machine in the room to make your own in-room espresso 鈥?perfect after a long flight. Our bags were sent to our room very quickly and there was a complimentary fruit platter and bottled water on arrival. Staying in a Club room allows you plus an invited guest entry to the Raffles Inc Lounge. This lounge offers breakfast from 6-10am (you can have breakfast at 2 other restaurant choices in the hotel if you want, but it is quieter in the lounge), from 10-5 tea/coffee/water/softdrinks and biscuits are available. From 5-8pm is happy hour 鈥?complimentary alcoholic beverages are available (beer, wine, champagne (Moet), top-shelf spirits (Johnnie Walker black, Skyy vodka, Bombay sapphire gin, Baileys etc) and hot and cold dishes changing daily. There is also a live cooking station with 2 hot dishes prepared to order, and a delicious selection of desserts. There is a free broadband internet terminal in the lounge, plus some magazines and other reading material. There is also a private gym on this level (23rd) for guests staying on the club floors.There are 2 swimming pools with sunlounges on the 8th floor. There is also the 鈥淎lligator Pear鈥?alfresco restaurant that overlooks the pool area 鈥?nice for breakfast.All of the staff that we encountered were very friendly and helpful. This is my second stay at this hotel and I will definitely stay here again next time I visit Singapore.

<Author>Brit-abroad-in-Asia
<Content>Functional! In my opinion, the Fairmont hotel is a functional business hotel. The rooms are not large, but are clean and the bathrooms are nice. <Content>New name but same quality experience... Recently stayed at the Fairmont Singapore for 3 nights. Have stayed at this hotel every year now since 2002 and athough the name has changed our experience has not. When I found out that the hotel had become a Fairmont (from previously being Raffles the Plaza and before that the Westin Plaza) I was slightly apprehensive about any potential changes, especially after reading some reviews, but can honestly say that we were as impressed as ever. If anything I think the customer service has gone up a notch - certainly in the lobby area the staff seemed more attentive. I always book through a local Singapore agent and have never experienced a problem with a booking and manage to obtain an all inclusive rate. I would strongly recommend booking a room in the South Tower as these are more modern and are well worth the extra few dollars. One of the many things I love about the Fairmont is that you can step outside your room onto the balcony and take in the atmosphere and city buzz from above and the views are just amazing. For someone who used to live in Singapore I think that the location is just perfect - shopping centre and MRT attached (just 3 stops to Orchard Rd), within walking distance to Suntec City, the Esplanade, Sim Lim, Bugis, Boat Quay, as well as all of the 'just over the road' places such as Raffles Hotel and Chijmes. I did pay more this year for the hotel but it seems that all hotel rates in Singapore have gone up and this one by no greater proportion than any other. Have also stayed at the Oriental Hotel, The Fullerton, Mandarin, Pan Pacific and others but keep coming back to the Fairmont. Can't wait for next years visit!  
<Date>Jun 22, 2008

<Author>MagdalenaH
<Content>Great Hotel Stayed at the Fairmont Singapore for work. The hotel was excellent from the time I checked in, to two weeks later when I checked out. The lobby is beautiful and relaxing. Reception was very friendly and quick. The room had plenty of space and was nicely appointed. Turn-down service every night and they set the music to classical so you feel really relaxed when you come back each night. The bed and pillows were very comfortable, and had great sheets. All lights / curtains are remote controlled. Excellent spa bathroom with great Miller Harris products, walk-in rainfall shower, over sized tub, and glass vanity/sink. Each room has a balcony. The hotel is directly attached to Raffles City shopping center and you can access the subway without leaving the building. Grocery store is located in the shopping center downstairs; very convenient for snacks. Nice gym. Great location: close to downtown, across from the Raffles Hotel (have a Singapore Sling at the Long Bar), and across from Chjmes. A couple of subway stops from Orchard Road. I was happy to return home after two weeks, but sad that I had to leave my beautiful hotel room!

<Content>Great location, reasonable hotel Overall we were happy with our stay, though it wasn't without a few niggles.We stayed en route to Sydney and New Zealand, for two nights. I booked when it was still Raffles the Plaza. Overall it worked out well for us at the rate we paid.Good:- upgraded due to hotel being busy and having booked early. So in North Tower, but on executive floor. We weren't allowed to use the executive lounge, but with our 11 year old so with us, this was fine.- room large, comfortable  clean. Great views from the high floor - over the Esplanade, part of the Padang and the city. - Location was great for us - across from Raffles (we had booked afternoon tea) and up from Suntec Mall where we did the Hippo tour from. Also walkable to National musuem.- Bell boy was very sweet to our son.Could have been better:- the room rate on check-in was more than on my reservation. After quite a while conferring with management, the original rate was confirmed.- there was no bed for our 11 year old, despite several emails after the initial booking to correct where this had got lost. On phoning reception they said that would be SIN $30 / night additional cost. When I'd returned to reception to show them my emails, again the original rate was finally agreed.- we went out to get food, but the bed wasn't there when we returned. In all, it probably took 3-4 hours for the bed to show up. After an overnight flight from London we finally got the bed at about 2300, having put our son to sleep in our bed.Singapore in general we really enjoyed. We would recommend:- Afternoon tea in the Tiffin room at Raffles. There were a couple of tour groups, but they sensitively sat smaller parties in a slightly separate area, which was nice. You are also encouraged to leave by the main lobby, which was a nice touch. Do book ahead though - we booked ages in advance (it was a Saturday). There definitely was no getting in on the day.- Night Safari- National Museum, including History of Singapore wing.

<Content>Raffles Inc. rooms very nice I stayed 5 nights in April 2008 at the Fairmont for a conference in the Raffles City Convention center. The overall experience was nice.Check InCheck in was fairly slow, but this was my first time to the hotel so they had no guest history, and they did upgrade me to a Raffles Inc. room.RoomThe room I had was spacious, well lit, and well laid out. It was nice to be on the Raffles Inc floor as the room had recently been renovated and one had access to the breakfast and evening snacks. I complained 3 days in succession about this, and I know that efforts were made to fix it, but this is an older property and while the rennovation was nice, it clearly didn't touch the a/c system. In fact most of the common areas of the hotel, the gym, and the restaurants were quite hot. Because I was only in the room to sleep, I never made a huge issue of it. TV channels in the room were very limited.GymThe gym was well equipped and had some of the latest Life Fitness equipment including ellipticals, treadmills, and cycles. It did have some older equipment as well. There was also a complete selection of weight machines and free weights.DiningDining in the hotel is nice, but quite expensive. Other options are readily availble in the basement of the attached mall, and across the street at Chijmes.LocationExcellent. Walking distance to a number of restaurants, and the attached mall is quite nice.I will stay here again, but I'll probably make certain that I get a room that will cool below 25C next time, and I probably won't risk anything other than the Raffles Inc. floor.

<Author>MariaPaula
<Content>Not a 5-star, but a good 4-star I stayed at the Fairmount in December 07 during 7 nights. Halfway through the week, it went from being called the Raffles Plaza to become the Fairmount.I stayed on the Raffles Inc. floor (25th or 26th floor) in the North Tower. It was a huge corner room with big 2 big balconies (1 towards CHIJMES and the other towards the Financial District) and great finishings. I did not see the issues other reviewers saw about tired carpeting and bathroom, everything looked renovated (and trust me that I looked).I expect to be blown away by 5-star hotels. This hotel is a 4-star level.The biggest complaint is that the internet service was not free. One had to call reception, get a code, enter it everyday (and some days it did not work, but we were reimbursed), and I don't remember the price but it was not cheap. For a high-tech country like Singapore, that is just ridiculous. Sure we had access to the internet in the business lounge, but who wants to wait around for a computer to free up and have people lurking around?I loved the mattress and the electronic controls in the room. A few disappointments when the hotel changed management: 1/ the bath supplies offered by Raffles were more exotic and luxurious than the ones offered by Fairmount, 2/ No more chocolates on my pillow! 3/The turndown service became less efficient.The breakfast and happy hour at the Raffles Inc lounge were phenomenal. All kinds of choices, and all delicious.The service was spotty. We noticed that some customers were mostly ignored, while others were served promptly. Luckily for us, we were always in the latter group. Some of the reception desk people were professional but cold, others were very helpful (I dislike over-the-top, fake American-style friendliness, but expect a minimum of assistance).Great location for everything, although it's faster to walk half a block to get a taxi rather than wait at the hotel door because the traffic blocks the entrance for the taxis.So overall very good, but not fabulous.

<Author>skyfriendbrighton
<Content>Sick of the North Tower... This is a huge hotel, linked to the Swissotel next door. The lobby has just been refurbed and is impressive. Unfortunately, it is effectively two hotels in one, the North tower and the South tower. The North tower (I am there now) is depressing and faded, with stained acrylic carpets, chipped sanitary ware and drab decor. The bed is really hard and uncomortable. I made mine bearable by using the bedlinen from the other bed in the room as an extra mattress pad. I mentioned this to the receptionist, and she said housekeeping would come to help. No-one came. The airconditioning cannot be controlled by temperature - only fan speed. It was really stuffy in the room and I woke up on my snooker table like bed bathed in perspiration. I have stayed here many times and the AC problem is immensely irritating as it is NEVER effective. There were hairs in the bathtub, and the satin coverlets were dirty. Room service was prompt, but the dish I ordered was not what I was expecting. I think this was my fault rather than theirs, but the items were not charged and there was no fuss either - so kudos for that. All rooms have balconies, but the sliding door doesn't fit well, resulting in traffic noise that requires earplugs. In summary;Rooms: Depressing, grubby, stuffy, beds like pool tables, noisy. Why bother? Better at a youth hostel. I bet the ones in Singapore are clean and well run.The South tower however, is superb, lovely beds, icy air-con, sparking bathrooms, Bose sound systems, flat screen TV, effective sound insulation - I loved staying there. On the Fairmont website there is no way of telling which tower you are in. Honestly, to stay in the North Tower is to waste your money. My company put me up here and I have had enough of it.

<Content>The Fairmont Singapore CHECK IN/OUTWas swift and efficient nothing to complain about. SPA: The spa is a Willow stream spa, which I believe is the signature spa of Fairmont, and its defiantly does not disappoint. It was a very relaxing experience, a little costly but you pay for what you get! My group all had the de stress massage and all commented on how much they enjoyed the experience and how professionally it was conducted.There are outdoor pools, they were busy bust still enjoyable.LOCATION:Very good, right in the heart of Singapore with all the amenities that you could possibly want right on your doorstep. The hotel is also located virtually in a transport hub with busses and trains and major roads all located very close by.ROOM:Was modern and well maintained, with all the mod cons that you would expect from a newer hotel in Asia. Plasma screen tv鈥檚 electric curtains etc. Bathroom was very nice with an amazing 鈥榬ainfall shower鈥? Room had high quality toiletries as you would expect.Always had a very good night鈥檚 sleep linen was of high quality as were the selection of pillows that were provided (Feather and synthetic) All rooms have small balconies that allow you to enjoy the atmosphere of the city.More than ample working space.No problems with noise.HOUSEKEEPING:This was an area that I felt needed some improvement. The room was in need of a good hovering under the bed etc and the windows did need washed. For the 3 nights that we were in the hotel our toiletries were never replenished which was disappointing .The room was always cleaned before 12 which was good. All in all the problems that we encountered were nothing too serious and when brought to the hotels attention was dealt with promptly. RESTAURANTS  BARS:Where to start there are so many outlets to choose from! The hotel is actually part of a large complex that also includes the Swissotel which is a staggering 70 floors high. Right at the top you have a selection of fantastic bars which have impressive views of the city. However the fine dinning restaurant equinox was a disappointment. The food was good but the service was poor. It took over 30 minutes for our drinks to arrive which is completely unacceptable in an outlet of this calibre. Here鈥檚 hoping that this was a one of event. The selection is good however we did have a few problems getting the right drinks on two mornings鈥?possible language problems鈥?they did however amend the problems very swiftly. They had all the Italian classics that you would expect and they were all of a very high quality. I would recommend this outlet for any occasion lunch, dinner or just a light snack. OVERALL:I thoroughly enjoyed my stay at the Fairmont Singapore. It has all the facilities that you would expect from a city hotel and an outstanding team of staff that will endeavour to make your stay as relaxing as possible. It is on the more expensive side but as always you do get what you pay for and I would highly recommend this hotel.

<Author>NoOneWillAnswer
<Content>Good Location Stayed three nights, south tower, facing CBD/Merlion. Recommend that room orientation for the views and sunrise/sunset. Good: Views. Immediate access to public transportation. Charging privileges at Raffles/Swissotel/Fairmont. Attached to shopping mall -- which includes a full grocery store with wine shop on the lower level, nice to be able to buy a piece of fruit or a bottle of wine whenever you want. Bakeries/food outlets also downstairs in the mall if you're jetlagged and looking for something small to grab-and-go. Breakfast buffet at the MarketPlace. Balcony. Speakers in bathroom for Bose. Pool.Bad: Three errors at checkin, requiring two follow-up calls and visits to the front desk to fix. One bedside reading lamp with a burned-out bulb, reported at checkin and again midstay, never replaced. Gooseneck reading lamp at the chaise wouldn't stay in place so was basically worthless. Front support leg of the chaise broken. Bathroom's glass basin is attractive but becomes very messy in use. Bathroom shower's glass enclosure is too shallow and bathroom floor floods unless you keep your body very close to the shower wall. Speakers in bathroom not hooked up to tv. Final insult was a SG$5 charge for the concierge desk to arrange a metered taxi to take us to the airport -- this after we paid SG$120 for the hotel's private arrival transfer. Have never been charged anywhere anytime for a concierge to get a taxi.

<Author>manarak
<Content>good for business I stayed a week on corporate rate at the fairmont south tower in a standard room in early february.what to say...let's start with possible improvements:- while about 10000 wireless access points in Singapore provide FREE internet access, it is high time that hotels do the same. Maybe they could limit the speed of the free access to 512kbps or something, but asking for more than 20SGD a day for that kind of commodity is not acceptable.- cleanliness: the room itself was quite nice, but it was not very clean. usually i am not very sensible to a little dust here and there, but the cleanliness of that room was sub-standard. for example, there was a lot of dust under the TV commode and it seemed that a guest had a bottle of coke or another sticky beverage explode on the table. the table itself had been cleaned, but the lamp and other parts of furniture were still dirty, as well as the floor where that happened (sticky dried-up drops).also in the bathroom, i would find a long dark hair everyday in the middle of the floor after room cleaning.mold between tiles in the bathroom is not much of a hygiene problem, but it would just look nicer if it was regularly bleached out (a few chlorine every 3-4 months could take care of that problem)the room cleaning staff is not thorough. additionally to finding dust and sticky stains in some places, I found two DVDs hidden by another guest under the bose radio. These were bad-quality porn DVDs, so I left them there.- room service/equipment: the staff should focus on better attention to detail: the remote command of the bose radio was missing the battery and therefore didn't work.- irritating: when you call a lift and briefly press the button, it will light up, but can deactivate if you are too quick. that happened a few times, and was quite irritating, especially because the button lit up, so i thought the life was coming...- while the bad's mattress was ok, I wasn't too satisfied with the pillows, which are apparently filled with a synthetic foam, which caused me to sweat.now the positive:- my request for a non-smoker king size room was granted without trouble.- the staff was quite friendly.- the hotel is situated right next to the historic raffles, and on top a shopping mall and above the MRT (underground) station city hall.- there are direct entrances from levels 2 and 3 of the mall into the elevators, so it is very convenient for getting quickly to the room from the mall without having to pass the lobby.- if you have to check out late, they can give you access to a complementary guest suite (no bed) to wait on your plane.- 2 bottles of water are replaced every day- i will not post a list of everything that worked as expected, you can assume the rest of standard services was provided and working well.Overall, the Fairmont was not bad to stay in for business, but I feel the rate was too high (even the corporate one) for the delivered quality. Therefore, the Fairmont gets a rating of 3 from me.

<Author>Global_traveller2000
<Content>Dear me, what happened here?! I dislike giving bad reviews, especially to such a lovely hotel that has been providing me with memorable stays throughout the years. It certainly wasn't very memorable this time, I can guess that this has something to do with the management change, lack of staff and too-full occupancy. I arrived from Changi at 4pm and waited at the entrance for the bellboy to come and collect my 6 pieces of luggage. No one came. The kind cab driver had to run in and call someone out to collect the luggage. Check-in was with a sour Indonesian receptionist who kept insisting that I should join some Fairmont Club Privilage Program although I kindly said I did not want to. In the end, she decided that I should join and she filled the membership form on my behalf (shocked!). OK, I thought, I'm only here for 3 days, thank goodness.I was given a Deluxe room on the 13th floor facing the Raffles Hotel. The room was called Premier Room the last time I stayed there, so no complaints there. The room was clean and comfy until I decided to take a shower. The toilettries used to be the wonderful Amrita Spa range of products (now called Willow Spa), but this time, they somehow managed to change it into a not-so-pleasant range called Citron by Harris Mueller London which smelled something like dishwashing liquid! Thank goodness I found a Body Shop downstairs and managed to grab a couple of items before I showered. If that wasn't the end of it, the water from the shower flooded the bathroom and I almost slipped and fell when I stepped out of the shower stall. Terribly bad design and choice of floor marble there, quite alike to the Traders Hotel in KL. I called housekeeping to clean the flood up and they were very apologetic and promised to bring this matter up to management. There were a few other problems that night, mainly the air-conditioning not working properly, resulting to a hot and stuffy night (the technician came the next morning to repair it) and there was a rather irritating man downstairs whistling the whole day and night for cabs to pull into the hotel. Since I couldn't possibly get a new room or a new hotel around CDB as everything was fully booked, I managed to spend quite a number of quiet nights at the Long Bar opposite and the City Space upstairs. Breakfast was still as good and quiet and the hotel's location is still great. My verdict: This wouldn't be a bad hotel if they managed to clean the management up, take in more staff to cope with the high occupancy and try to maintain a bit of its Asian image instead of trying to push the hotel to achieve Fairmont London image. Too much change is still worse than no change. I might give this hotel another try if things improve, since I owe Raffles the Plaza most of my best stays in Singapore.  
<Date>Feb 13, 2008

<Author>adls
<Content>Great location, decent hotel, shame about the room cleaning (or lack of it) We stayed here on a 4-day family holiday with our baby. We had previously stayed at the Swissotel the Stamford which is actually in the same hotel-shopping mall complex as the Fairmont. We liked the Swissotel for its great location, and decided to stay at the Fairmont this time because we had a better deal for it on Expedia and it was essentially the same location.The Fairmont is quite a businessman鈥檚 hotel: it鈥檚 smart, clean and efficient 鈥?but somehow lacks character and charisma. The building, lobby, elevators and rooms are all modern, clean, relatively spacious, but you don鈥檛 get much of a sense of occasion or opulence. There鈥檚 nothing grand or magnificent about the d茅cor, just functionality. In that sense, I would say this is better suited for those in suits, and maybe less so for those expecting a romantic or exotic holiday.The room was quite large by Asian hotel standards. There was room enough for a cot for baby to be moved in (at no extra cost) and yet leave absolutely plenty of room for all 3 of us (mainly baby) to run around. And the cot was not a flimsy little crib, but a large proper baby鈥檚 bed with baby blankets and even a gift soft toy 鈥?nice touch. The furniture was again functional rather than grand or elegant, but at least the chairs were comfortable. The bed was definitely on the firm side 鈥?which I personally like, but which may probably not be to everyone鈥檚 tastes. The pillows were agreeably large and long, but they were too soft and shapeless and failed to give good support. I appreciated the cleanliness, but the room did show some wear and tear in places: the cold water faucet leaked a little when turned on, and the carpet was well worn down in the middle of the room (even patched over in one place).The service at the front door is excellent. The porters are exceptionally warm and courteous, and instantly made us feel welcome as we stepped out of the taxi from the airport. Check-in was efficient and reasonably friendly too. Throughout our stay, I was also impressed with being greeted by name every time I called down to the front desk (or 鈥極n-call Valet鈥?as they like to call it).Unfortunately, the good service did not extend to the room cleaners. We stayed for 4-days/3-nights. During that time, we only had our room cleaned ONCE. On one day, we were out almost all morning but came back to the room briefly at around 2pm to get a change of clothes (Singapore is a hot, humid country). The room was not cleaned all morning. We left promptly after changing and did not return until after dinner. But when we got back, not only had the room still not been cleaned, but we got a little note under our door saying that it wasn鈥檛 cleaned because we had a 鈥楧o Not Disturb鈥?sign on the door for the brief period while we were changing. After retiring to our room exhausted after a day out with baby, the last thing we wanted to do was vacate the room again at night while we called the cleaners back for cleaning (assuming anyone was still around to clean after 5pm !). Altogether we received this irresponsible little card on TWO days during our stay, suggesting it was OUR fault that the room wasn鈥檛 cleaned. This is unacceptable. Why can鈥檛 hotels like this just get their act together and clean the room quickly during the day? Is it unreasonable to expect that at a world class hotel, if the cleaner finds your room occupied when she comes round then she will check again later a second or third time until finally each room on her floor is cleaned? Since when has it become OK to just see a 鈥楧o Not Disturb鈥?sign once and assume the room cannot be cleaned at any other time of the day? Couldn鈥檛 someone simply have politely phoned us in the room to ask when would be a good time for them to clean the room? Sadly, the Fairmont is not the only hotel I鈥檝e stayed in recently to suffer from this lazy attitude towards room cleaning 鈥?but I really would鈥檝e expected better from a decent hotel in a country like Singapore. Having an uncleaned room for half our stay certainly spoiled our stay a fair bit.We didn鈥檛 have breakfast in our package. If you like eating, you don鈥檛 come to Singapore for bacon and eggs ! Downstairs in the Raffles City Mall alone, you can find a great variety of eateries. Try Kaya Toast, Singapore-style soft boiled eggs, and Kopi-O for a proper local breakfast. The Mall is also directly connected via an underground 鈥榗ity鈥?to the MRT station and nearby attractions like the Esplanade and Suntec City. Raffles Hotel (home of the Singapore Sling), Chijmes, the old civic center are all literally just across the street. Orchard Road or Chinatown are both just a couple of stops away on the MRT. This convenience of location is exactly what we loved about the Swissotel on our previous trip, and what makes staying here at the Fairmont this time brilliant. With our baby along this time, we really appreciated having a supermarket and some drug stores downstairs so that we could buy all the usual baby products (formula milk, diapers etc) instead of having to carry huge amounts on the flight.We didn鈥檛 use the hotel鈥檚 facilities much. We were too busy seeing Singapore, tasting its excellent food, visiting the world-famous Zoo, shopping on Orchard Road and so on to bother with the swimming pool etc (we didn鈥檛 even bother finding out where the pool was). If you want to enjoy a hotel like a resort, the Fairmont probably isn鈥檛 the place for you. If you want a hotel as a convenient base for you to see this remarkable island, then I would recommend this hotel (or the Swissotel) 鈥?with the condition that they sort out their room cleaning service. There was a cable internet connection in the room, but there was a charge. I usually rely heavily on the internet during my trips, but as this was a purely family holiday and the charge looked rather steep, I resisted the urge to use this service on this trip.

<Content>Consistently Good Stayed at the Fairmont Singapore for three nights recently. <Author>SwedishCath
<Content>Wonderful stay We stayed at the newly named Fairmont hotel for 9 nights over Christmas and New Year. Overall we were impressed and enjoyed every aspect of our stay. Our room in the South Tower was modern and well kept with a lovely view towards the Marina Bay allowing us to watch the New Year fireworks from our balcony. The bathroom was large and light and the shower fantastic. The amenities were generously replenished thoughout our stay.It was a luxury having our room serviced twice a day with fresh towels and robes and new sheets on the bed every morning.The in room safe was large enough for our laptop and other valuables.It is a shame that the previous reviewer JamesVki did not ask about breakfast. We had breakfast in the hotel every morning (included in our room rate), either at their Market Plaza restaurant on the 2nd floor or by the pool on the 8th floor. Both breakfast buffets were extensive with western and asian choices. We preferred the Market Plaza because the staff were more attentive and the selection wider.We found the reception staff and the concierge to be very polite and helpful. I used them for a number of queries about Singapore. It was also possible to reserve a table in one of the numerous hotel restaurants by using the in room reservation service on the phone.The food and drinks in the hotel are not cheap but not outrageous by Singapore standards. Raffles Hotel next door was even more expensive (unsurprisingly). If you want to eat cheaper then there are plenty of options in the food court in the mall under the hotel. Also Chinatown had excellent food at excellent prices.The location of the hotel is perfect. We were in walking distance to Marina Bay, Clarke Quay, Suntec City and of course Raffles Hotel. The MRT under the hotel was very convenient for trips to other sites around the island. We can recommend going to the races at Singapore Turf Club, a 40 minute ride on the MRT. Book a package at their restaurant @hibiscus and enjoy a fantastic view of the races.All in all I would recommend this hotel to anyone visiting Singapore. Excellent rooms, good service, perfect location and a reasonable price.

<Author>Scousie
<Content>Great Stay at Raffles the Plaza We stayed at Raffles the Plaza for three nights on our outbound stopover to Australia. We paid 拢90 per room including breakfast booked through asiabesthotels.com (this website is great!).  It was our first time in Singapore and the hotel was a great choice. The City Mall is underneath offering a huge selection of shops and eating - we were still finding floors we didn't know about on our last day! There's a bank as well which is really convenient and lots of beauty places for a bit of a pamper. There's another mall linking the City Mall to the Suntec Mall which we didn't find out about til our return trip!The City Hall MRT station is right underneath the hotel as well which is really convenient. We used this to go to the Singapore Zoo and it also goes direct to the Airport. The hotel itself was very nice and was excellent value for money. The room was spacious and the beds were really comfy. We had a small balcony overlooking the city with nice views. Staff were pleasant and helpful and there is also a hospitality room made available to guests either arriving early or leaving late with a shower, tv etc which is really convenient if you arrive at 7am and have a midnight flight out as I did!Breakfast was a buffet with a wide range of food in european, asian and american styles, available til 11am and very nice. Pool was lovely!Overall this was a really good, convenient, modern hotel with all the facilities you would expect from a decent 4 star. Would definately consider this hotel again when visiting Singapore.

<Content>Great Hotel I stayed at Raffles the Plaza for 1 night this week. It was a short trip, taken at short notice. I called the hotel just 2 hours before I got on the plane to Singapore, and their reservations staff were very helpful and got me what turned out to be a very nice room at a reasonable rate. The location indeed, is excellent, particularly on a short trip, because it is right off of the highway to the airport. The attractive lobby looked much nicer than the last time I stayed, back right in the aftermath of SARS in June 2003.The front desk staff was very helpful and efficient. She also remembered my name when I checked out 7 hours later. The room was large, well appointed, and had a generous portion of fruit for my consumption, which came in handy after the subpar airplane food and the late night of work I had ahead (there was also chocolate). Shower worked beautifully, and the bed very comfortable. The breakfast the next day also hit the spot, with a nice mix of local specialties in addition to well-rendered international staples.Would definitely stay again.

<Author>Malingshu
<Content>Great location I stayed in Raffles the Plaza for 5 nights on a business trip and was very pleased with the quality of the room, service and location. Breakfast was booked as part of the room rate and was well worth it - a good selection of Asian and European food. The cafe at the pool also does a less extensive breakfast menu but the location is lovely if you want to get away from the airconditioning. On the advice of previous reviewers I booked the South Tower and would recommend this because of the views over the city and Straits. Most windows in the North Tower look into buildings. The best thing about Raffles the Plaza is its location above the MRT station and shopping centre. Having also recently stayed in Orchard Road, I would recommend staying here instead because the streets are less crowded and there is more green open space.

<Author>reddygirl
<Content>wow! excellent stay and benefits although this a belated review, my husand and i stayed there for our 10th anniversary (a little late, but we got there) in 2004. a lovely experience from start to finish. we booked through qantas holidays, and received the club floor upgrade, which, when we looked back at all the extras we recieved, was superb value. check in was efficient. staff gave the air of being well trained and polite. i found them at all times through out stay to be very friendly also.breakfast was in the club room, with no kids, and efficient service with a smaller choice than downstairs (which was tried once for the variety however was too noisy) but still marvellous. lovely coffee and the food was of excellent quality. pastries were superb! what a surprise when we arrived for the afternoon cocktails and canapes! in fact, i still rave about them three years later! veuve cliqot champagne, top shelf spirits and as for canapes, no soggy cheese and biscuits here, there were hot canapes, french cheeses, juices of all varieties, all sorts of cold canapes, beautiful desserts plus more, and well, we certainly gave the champagne a good go! in fact, we only ate out twice at night when we were there, and regretted it as we were so full from the food at the hotel! the room was lovely and we were given a note congratulating us on our anniversary, lovely fruit, and chocolates in wooden boxes (which were superb, i'm a raging chocoholic and i still have the boxes!) each night, along with turndown service of dimmed lights, linen folded down and soft music playing, which was just amazing. plenty of bottled water was supplied each day. the marble bathroom was divine with a fantastic rain shower and excellent toiletries. the location was terrific, having a shopping centre attached to the hotel complexes. visited the vertigo bar next door at swissotel (where i stayed in 2007, see another review) a tip - go during happy hour (singapore people seem to arrive much later) and the bar was crowded with aussies, poms and kiwis. the cocktails while a little expensive are reasonable during happy hour and are fabulous. the view is recommended!.(we also visited raffles for a singapore sling. expensive, but am not sure i thought raffles was any better than where we were) the pool was a welcome retreat in the heat of singapore. quiet when we were there and wonderfully clean.getting taxis was not a problem as they were waved down by staff and we never had to wait more than a very short while. we did not find the location a problem, as singapore is not a very large place and i felt everything was in short reach. chijmes was around the corner and has several terrific eating places and shops there.check out was as check in, with marvellous staff and no problems. they even tried to locate something i wanted to buy, nothing seemed to be any trouble.in short, the best hotel i have ever stayed at in my life. nothing so far has topped it - (but surprisingly the swissotel, whilst not as flashy, is almost as excellent). a lovely ambience, terrific staff, excellent facilities, superb service, terrific location, a very classy well run feel all round.just a joy to stay at.i have told my husband i want to go back!

<Author>Wine_Gums_Addict
<Content>Book a club room!!! Fab fab fab hotel - great location, service and facilities. Can't fault it at all.We stayed here for 3 nights en route back to London from Australia during our honeymoon. As it was our honeymoon we booked into a club room which was well worth it as we got delicious complimentary breakfast in the plaza club lounge each day and fab 'free' cocktails, proper French champagne and canapes each night from 5pm to 8pm. A further nice touch was that we were offered to use the lounge for cocktails etc in the evening even after we'd checked out. Check out time is 1pm standard which is better than the usual 11am or 12 noon.We were put in a corner room on the 25th floor which was amazing as we had dual aspect double balconies, a large lounge area, large bed, desk area etc, and the usual robes, slippers etc. Also we had champers, chocs, fruit and flowers - don't know whether this was standard or because we were honeymooners.The facilities at this hotel are fantastic and the service top notch. I would not hesitate to stay there again or recommend it to anyone . It is quite a 'businessy' hotel but although we were on our honeymoon we still thought it was fab and much better than some of the more traditional 5 star honeymoon hotels we'd stopped at in Oz. The inc bar on the ground floor is fab, and the hotel is connected to the Swissotel Stamford the Plaza via the Raffles City shopping mall, which is good to go to for dinner or drinks from the 72nd floor - apparently the tallest hotel in Asia. The location was fab, v central, opposite the old Raffles hotel. Taxis and the fab MRT are very cheap in Sing though so everything is at your doorstep when you need it. I'd recommend the Night Safari and a trip to Sentosa to go to Underwater World which was great. Also Clarke Quay is great for bars and restaurants, try Clinic, and have a go at the reverse bungy if you're an adrenaline seeker...

<Author>iamallovertheplace
<Content>Great hotel in the centre of everything Stayed here for 5 nights and had a room overlooking the memorial and across the cricket pitch to downtown. There is a lot to like about this hotel, the rooms are big and have everything you need, with a great bathroom. The lobby is attached to a shopping mall where there are numerous places to eat, either Western or Oriental food, including a new donut shop, where the queues are extraordinary. There is pleasant pool area on the 8th floor, with two small pools. It is quite a restricted place, so you may need to get there early if you want a lounger.The hotel is in a good spot - you can walk to most places - Orchard Road is 15 mins away or a hop on the MRT. The old Raffles hotel is across the road and you should try the entertainment on the top floors of the Swiss Hotel next door - the views are great, especially at night.You can't go far wrong in Singapore - the top hotels are all very good and this is no exception - certainly worth a stay.

<Author>MollyCardiff
<Content>Fantastic - perfect hotel in perfect location We booked 3 nights in a Premier Deluxe room in the South Tower en route to Australia on the strength of reviews from this site, and then 2 nights in the Pan Pacific on the way back (please see separate review).Raffles the Plaza met all of my (high) expectations - Check-in at around 9.30pm was friendly and efficient. Room no. 1439 overlooking the pool with views over to the city and the bay to the left was as good as has been described on this site - huge comfy bed, gorgeous bathroom (the reviewer who complained about the rainfall shower flooding needed to just put the shower mat down!) and lots of little touches (fab Raffles branded toiletries you can buy in the real Raffles shop across the road for expensive prices). No furniture on the balcony (this seems to be the norm in Singapore) but we sat on towels drinking beer and watching the world go by. Fab.We had Breakfast included in our room rate and ate at the Plaza Market Cafe on floor 2 - amazing choice of just about anything you might want, probably the best hotel breakfast I've ever had.I tried the room service one evening and again, great choice, excellent service, not too bad prices.We had massages in the Amitri Spa, quite pricy but fantastic - try the lovely ginger tea they offer you as you are taking to the relaxation room before and after the treatment. Obviously staying mid week there are a lot of business travellers, but the hotel appears to cater equally for tourists, which was different to our experience at the Pan Plaza.We managed to squeeze a lot of sightseeing into a short space of time and I don't think you can beat the location of this hotel for being central to all of the main sites. Opposite Raffles, walking distance to the bay, Boat Quay and Clarke Quay (both great in the evening), the business district, China Town, Chijmes (gorgeous in the evening, restaurants all lit up with fairy lights and live music), Orchard Road (a bit of a trek, but easy on the MRT) etc. etc.Don't miss seeing the view from the 72nd floor of the hotel next door, the Swisshotel, (connected to RtP by walkways).My other 'must do' sights were: 1. Night Safari (you can get a tourist bus from outside one of the hotels on Orchard Room - look at their website, or a taxi is less than $20)2. The Zoo (the best zoo I have ever been too, lots of the animals are roaming freely, but safely! - so cleverly done). I wouldn't suggest you do the Zoo and the Night Safari in the same day unless you are v. fit and used to the humidity - exhausting).3. The cable car ride to Sentosa, and then up to Mount Faber (Sentosa itself ok for a day trip - we saw everything we wanted to see in a few hours -I was pleased I hadn't booked to stay there).4. Walking through the streets of ChinaTown - a refreshing change from the millions of malls all over the city. Don't stick just to the main tourist streets.Overall, I was throughly impressed with Singapore - it's not the sterile boring city some people have said at all. I'd love to go back one day, and will definitely stay at Raffles the Plaza if I do.

<Author>Nonnapn
<Content>Business meets Pleasure The Raffles The Plaza is right across the street from the old Raffles Hotel and while you may prefer the other for its significant history and its colonial ambiance, this hotel is pure sheer quiet elegance and superb service.The lobby while not as brightly welcoming or bustling as the neighboring Swissotel The Stamford, gives off a subdued and comforting feeling. Reception and check in are handled well and quickly -- even if there is queue, someone quickly steps up and attends to you immediately. The front desk staff are efficient and professional.The rooms, specially those in the newer wing are very modern and furnishings are classy and yet extremely comfortable. I have stayed in their premier executive rooms which have large walk in closets, a very inviting divan with a reading lamp -- just the place to lounge around in when reading or watching something on the very new lcd t.v.The bathrooms are huge and come with a bathtub and a separate shower stall with an overhead rain shower -- so great for relaxing after a long business day --Just like its sister property, The Swissotel Stamford, which it is connected to, Raffles The Plaza shares the same restaurants and mall and is very conveniently located beside the City Hall MRT station. I have noticed that most of those staying at the Raffles The Plaza are businessmen and corporate types -- now that is really mixing business with pleasure!

<Author>SamSteel
<Content>Overall a Good Hotel, Some Inconveniences The rooms are nicely decorated, and there are many conveniences with the Spa and Fitness center conveniently located downstairs and the Fitness facility is very well equiped and open for hotel guests during off hours. I really enjoy their Yoga classes which are reasonably priced at $15 SIN. The rooms are very well cleaned (in the morning with turndown service in the evening). They keep filling the ice bucket in the evening even after I told the manager not to bother with it. I think they want to tempt me into using some of the overpriced minibar drinks. The only complaint I have about the room is that there is no door on half the shower stall, and the rain water shower invariably ends up splashing out of the shower a getting the whole bathroom floor wet. A real inconvenience as I am here for work, and just want a quick - hassle free shower in the morning. The internet service was also a real dissapointment. They advertise the Superior room with Internet Access. Access = Pay For Use. And pay you will at about $30 SIN per day. The hotel is in a great area and within easy walking distance from Chinatown for those late nights out, Suntec City and other spots of interest. The MRT is conveniently located in Raffles Plaza.

<Author>IanWriter
<Content>Excellent hotel This is an excellent hotel. I found the staff to be friendly and efficient. The room was are a generous size, the bed was comfortable, the furnishings and decor well thought out, the min bar was well stocked, the bathrooms were beautifully designed and well equipped, and the restaurants were very good indeed. There is a neat bedside console that controls everything from AC and lights to alarm clock and remote conrol of the window curtains. Overall, the hotel has that certain blandness of style common to virtually all high end hotels of this type -- lots of marble, wood paneling, and beige as the dominant color -- but that seems to be what the clients are comfortable with.The one gripe I have is that the hotel charges a daily rate for internet access. As a general rule, the cheaper the hotel, the more likely it is to provide internet for free, and the more expensive the hotel, the more likely it is to treat internet access as a profit center and pile on the charges. A backpacker dive can be counted on to provide free interent but the deluxe hotels of the world dont give it away for free!

<Author>TanyaMumOfTwo
<Content>Loved location and rooms! Customer service nothing special. Our family (myself husband and two large teenagers) have just returned from a wonderful trip to Singapore. I will be posting a Trip Report on the forum in the coming days but thought I'd do hotel reviews first.My agent originally had us booked into the Pan Pacific but when she received notification of soft furnishing renovations at the time of our visit to the Pan Pac she recommended that we stay elsewhere. Based on TA reviews, the location, plus a very good rate that gave us our fourth night free and included breakfast, we booked a King and Twin (connecting) at Raffles The Plaza. The excellent location of this very elegant hotel cannot be praised too highly. With divine views over the Esplanade and the harbour to the Merlion (we were in the South Tower, Premier Deluxe Rooms, Level 19) opening the curtains from the master switches next to your bed each morning was exciting in itself! Walking out onto the small balcony an adventure!Situated above Raffles City Shopping Centre and the City Hall MRT station meant that most of Singapore was within easy reach. We had created our own itinerary and these four days whilst at Raffles The Plaza gave us easy access for our first four days of self made touring.The rooms were very spacious with ALL the mod cons, decorated in my favourite soothing shades and with very comfortable beds and bedding. A big plus for us was the couch/chaise at the end of the bed so one of the children could comfortably stretch out on it while we other three lay on the bed watching a TV show together before bed.The buffet breakfast each morning was a real treat and the smiling staff were professional and attentive. The offerings changed slightly each of the four mornings and with such an extensive choice we were never bored. Only minor issue was that the tea was never actually really hot. I'm not sure if it was the actual urn of water used, or the solid silver teapots that were then used on the tables.The pool area was clean and inviting with towels on offer and carried to our lounge chairs for us. A dip in the beautiful round pool at the end of a hot day was always welcome. We used the area only twice - once late in the afternoon and on another day well after our return from dinner. It was never crowded or noisy as the twin pool is the shallow version and if there were any younger children then that pool is where they swam.So my only real complaint is that of a lack of customer service from the front desk staff. Their attention was robotic at best and harrassed at worst. We arrived at 10pm as expected so the lobby was not busy. I had had a very bad start to our holiday with my British husband not being allowed to leave Australia with us due to not having a Re-entry Visa (this is a whole other story!!!). So it was just myself and the two children checking in - not knowing if my husband was actually ever going to be able to join us I was a bit tired and teary - and I explained what had happened to the girl as she was completing our check in procedures. I received a sympathetic smile and that was about it! Now I wasn't looking for anything major but where the Qantas cabin crew had gone out of their way to help me (and I will be writing a letter to Qantas complimenting them on their customer service) the staff at this hotel barely seemed to care. Maybe this sort of thing happens all the time and they were immune - but I think they should have picked up on my signals and been a little more caring.Then really the only other time I had anything to do with the staff was breakfast in the restaurant on the 2nd Floor as recommended here on TA (terrific), pool guy (attentive), luggage guy (great) and then check out (awful!). It was busy - about a 15 minute wait at approx 12 noon - but only had two staff on so not good enough. She rushed me through (as we had no extras to pay for) and I don't even think I received a thank you for choosing Raffles the Plaza! Just not what one would expect from such an otherwise professional and tasteful hotel. This front desk area is what is letting them down and I think you can see that here on other TA reviews. Having said that, I would still recommend this hotel if you can get a good rate as the rooms are generous and this location at the bay end is superb (I might just point out here that the last two nights of our trip when we were doing all our Orchard Road shopping were spent at the other end of town at Royal Plaza on Scotts and I will post another review for that hotel tomorrow night!). Look out for my trip report and feel free to PM me if you have any questions. Cheers

<Author>J0ey
<Content>We were so looking forward to this trip however ...... We love Singapore and visit at least once a year.There is no doubt that this is an above average hotel in a great position however customer service really let this hotel down.I have watched with interest the steady flow of positive reviews and have given a lot of thought as to why our experience was so different. I think the length of our stay was the contributing factor.We stayed for longer than the average guest,instead of the usual 2 or 3 nights we were booked in for nearly 3 weeks. After the first few nights the cracks began to show.We upgraded to the executive package which meant we could have breakfast and evening drinks/snacks in the Executive Club.Despite staying for nearly 21 nights not one staff member remembered our name or indeed used it while we were in the club. We were mostly ignored in the club and attended to our own drinks whilst watching the manager and other staff focus all of their attention on other guests (regulars of the hotel).The reception staff could be best described as surly and at times everything seemed too much trouble. Even when enquiring about a service listed in the in room brochure, staff would stare blankly and claim they did not know what you were talking about.On the positive side:The rooms are hard to match in a hotel of this price bracket in Singapore. The room was very well appointed. The bathroom was a delight and included a rain drop shower which was a novelty. We also enjoyed the in room coffee machine and CD player.The view was spectacular and the location is so central you could almost ignore the customer service problems if you are staying a short period of time.The pool has a limited number of deck chairs and it can be hard to secure one during the busier periods of the day. The pool facilites are shared with the Swiss Hotel next door, a large number of airline staff stay at this property and spend a lot of time at the pool. My advice is to arrive early and enjoy the pool before heading off to the shops etc which tend to open at 10 or 11 am.Unfortunately the poor customer service extends to the Pool Bar staff and those working in the health centre.If you are staying less than a week, want a great room with a great view, close to all Singapore has to offer this is the hotel for you .....just don't expect the customer service to meet or exceed your expectations. If you intend to be out and about a lot this hotel probably isn't worth the extra money as there are many hotels with good views and central locations nearby.So overall I agree the property itself is great it is just so disappointing that the service was so bad I have been prompted to write this review and that we did not enjoy this trip as much as my other annual trips to this great city.  
<Date>Jun 10, 2007

<Author>Jemimagold
<Content>Cannot say enough good things about Raffles the Plaza Hotel! We originally had planned to stay at the Le Meridien in Singapore for our recent 3 night stay there (see my TripAdvisor review of that). After the 2nd night at Le Meridien, we could not tolerate all the problems and so I got out my trusty Frommer's guidebook and booked us into the Raffles the Plaza Hotel for the last night (May 28th). I am so glad I did!The hotel lobby is decorated in a stylish Asian chic manner and our room was incredible. We booked just a regular room and got a very large room in the North Tower with a balcony which had all the latest technological gadgets such as a flat screen TV, halogen reading lights on flexible metal arms above the bed (in addition to lamps) for nighttime reading, a huge bathroom and the excellent toiletries from their spa. The hotel's gym was spacious, modern and clean. Breakfast was included in our room rate which we had at the Alligator Pear restaurant which is their outdoor pool restaurant (quite pleasant in the morning). There was a huge selection of healthy food as well as the usual hot breakfast items such as sausages, eggs, bacon, oatmeal, etc... It was all excellent. We also liked the fact that the hotel was so well located in the very center of town. It was very easy to take the metro anywhere we wanted to go and in fact, we even took the metro to the airport as the Hotel is on the same line. The sister Raffles Hotel property was directly across the street (which everyone must see!) and the charming CHIJMES restaurant/shopping complex was diagonally opposite the Raffles the Plaza as well.I am a pretty picky traveler and I have only wonderful things to say about this hotel. It is no question that I would stay here if/when I return to Singapore.

<Author>MelieL
<Content>Best location in Singapore! Very central Stayed at Raffles The Plaza on a business trip. What a top hotel! It's located directly above the MRT station, which is by far the easiest way to get around Singapore. It's not too far from some of the nicest places to eat (Boat Quay, Clarke Quay etc) and is a short MRT ride from Little India and Chinatown. What really impressed me was the service. When I arrived straight after leaving my other hotel, still quite annoyed that I had a disagreement with their staff which took well over an hour to sort out, I was told there was only a twin room available (rather than a king room, which I had booked). The staff member asked would this be ok? and I said not really, no. A minute later he had booked me into a corner suite, a brilliant room! It overlooked Raffles Hotel, had a huge lounge/business area, the bathroom was huge with a big, round bathtub and shower. There were two balconies, very generous toiletries, an amazingly comfortable bed and fluffy slippers replaced daily. The hotel adjoins Swissotel the Stamford and Raffles City which is a huge shopping centre, where the food court has some of the best Hainanese Chicken Rice ever. The only thing slightly less than perfect was the swimming pool, not very exciting for this class of hotel but good all the same.

<Author>bkkgal
<Content>Great Location; well-appointed rooms We stayed at Raffles the Plaza last month. The location was unbeatable! The hotel is within the Raffles City (shopping mall) complex and on top of the City Hall MRT, which makes getting around so easy. Plus the transportation system in Spore is so efficient. At 58sqm, the room was big and spacious. The bed is plush and heavenly. There was a writing desk, with internet connection (pay to use) and the rain shower in the bathroom is a nice treat to come back to after a long day. We took a room in the South Tower, which had a great view of the Esplanade at the bay front. There was even a Bose system in the room, which went off 3 times in the middle of the night on our first night! But other than that, everything was great.The breakfast buffet spread is astounding, with Western, Asian, Japanese and continental selections. My favourite was the fresh juices that we can customise e.g. carrot-orange-apple, celery-greenapples-carrots etc, from the counter. There are some 11 dining establishments in the hotel, we didn't get to try them all but it's good to have that choice. The staff is friendly and professional. Overall, a good place to stay in.

<Author>walkaboutnyc
<Content>Good choice: comfortable, decent price, great location I struggled a lot with my hotel choice in Singapore - trying to find a good mix of price, location, cleanliness, etc from the reviews on TripAdvisor and deals on various websites. We ended up at the Raffles Plaza, because I read in Frommers online that it was nicely located and it got good reviews here. It was a bit more than I wanted to pay in Singapore, given that there are so many hotels, but it turned out to be worth it.First of all, the woman who checked us in was so friendly and accommodating. We only had one night booked with a very late (midnight) flight the next day. She agreed to give us a late check out of 4pm...which I felt was really generous and kind! I have never been granted such a late checkout at any other hotel.The location IS good, as long as you don't mind being attached to a mall (most hotels in Singapore are close, if not attached, to shopping anyway). We walked from our hotel to the Boat Quay, then on to the Asian Civilizations Museum, over to Orchard Road (shopping area) and back in a little more than a half a day at a lesiurely pace. There is a lot of foot traffic in the hotel. Seemingly a lot of business people, but that didn't bother us at all. Our room was nice, nothing incredibly special but clean and overlooking the Raffles Hotel.Another benefit of the Plaza: the Amrita spa is amazing. I had a wonderful facial, the gym is great, and the variety of services, products (Dermologica) and amenities at the spa are excellent. They didn't rush me out at all, which I also liked very much and felt was different than some other spas I've been to recently.You could pay a lot more and I think a lot less in Singapore for a hotel. But the Raffles was just really comfortable and middle of the range in price, and so a real winner for my husband and me.

<Author>Vardomannen
<Content>The Problem with Singapore... ..OK, so it's one of those problems you might prefer to label a luxury problem - and that problem is, where to stay in Singapore if you really appreciate quality. Not because it is hard to find, but because there are so many 5 star hotels in this wonderful city that you may not know where to start. I've recently tried the Oriental and the Intercontinental and now this trip stayed at Raffles the Plaza - just to try something different, as I have no complaints at all about the aforementioned hotels.Raffles the Plaza lived up to all my expectations - and then some. The hotel is in the colonial district of town, leaving you 5 minutes walk to the marina area and 15 minutes to Orchard Road (although it is hot in Singapore and all that bag carrying on the way back from the shops may wear you out....and oh yes, you will be carrying bags because you won't be able to resist the choice and prices...). The rooms are calming; light brown walls, a liberal use of textiles as panelling keeping noise in the room to a minimum (and you won't hear a squeek from your neighbours). I was in the South Tower on the 11th floor; my room had a balcony, a flat-screen TV and a funky bathroom with huge showerhead and toiletries from the spa at the hotel. It goes without saying perhaps that the room was spotlessly clean. Most of Singapore is spottlessly clean. A dream for us clean freaks.The hotel also has a hospitality lounge where you can get a shower before your flight home. A nice touch, particularly when you are so lucky as I was to have a flight at 0100. Breakfast was served in the Stamford Hotel next door which is reached via an inside link. The selection at breakfast was enormous - local specialities, western favourites - you name it.So now I have a problem - and that problem is, which hotel should I stay in next time I go to Singapore. Raffles the Plaza is way up there - one of the big boys in town. I think that it is the price of the stay which will help me make my decision.

<Author>farrj
<Content>A great place to stay in Singapore We stayed at this excellent hotel for one night on our journey to Australia, and for two nights on our return journey.The hotel lives up to its 5 star rating, and is well situated in an established part of Singapore directly across the road from the original Raffles Hotel.The entrance to the hotel is impressive and from the moment you arrive, porters are there to help with your luggage. The hotel reception is equally impressive and spacious and the reception staff are friendly and efficient.Our rooms were in the North Tower on the 21st and 22nd floors with amazing views over the city. The rooms are spotlessly clean and very well equipped and furnished, down to bedside remote control units for curtains, lighting, air-conditioning etc. The rooms have safes (complimentary), bath robes, slippers, tea / coffee and a well stocked reasonably priced mini bar. The bathrooms are excellent with white marble tiles and glass fittings, including a bath and adjacent wet shower area incorporating a raindrop shower.We had the opportunity on our return stay to upgrade to Raffles INC and for a small additional payment we were able to use the Executive Lounge on the 23rd floor where a very good breakfast was served between 6.30am and 10.30am and also where cocktails and canapes were served between 5.00pm and 8.00pm - a very nice start to the evening!The hotel has several good restaurants and it is also possible to take meals in the original Raffles Hotel and charge them to your room (reservations needed).The hotel also include the Amrita Spa which has excellent facilities.We would thoroughly recommend this hotel and we intend to return in the not too distant future.

<Author>Happynoodleboy_uk
<Content>Loved it, great location Booked this hotel via Asiarooms. Took about 25 mins to get there in a taxi from Singapore Changi Airport, cost was about 20 SGD. Checked in with no problems, and was allocated a deluxe room on the 8th floor in the North Tower. Room was a great size, with a big king size bed, small balcony overlooking Raffles Hotel, mini bar, safe, iron/ironing board, TV, and electronically operated curtains. Bathrobe and slippers were also provided. Bathroom was a nice size, and with plenty of Amrita Spa toiletries. These were replenished twice a day, along with fresh towels twice a day and bed was turned down on a night.Two nice sized pools, although didn't get much opportunity to use them thanks to a tropical downpour! Lots of sunbeds available and it looked like it got the sun on a morning.Two choices of places to go for breakfast, either the Alligator Pear by the pool or the Market Plaza Cafe on the 2nd floor. We opted for the latter thanks to reviews on Tripadvisor and weren't disappointed. Great selection of chinese, japanese, and american breakfasts, plus fruit, cakes, juice bar, egg/pancake chefs. The choice was overwhelming.Hotel has good location in Raffles City shopping centre, right above the City Hall MRT station so it's a good base for exploring Singapore.The New Asia Bar on the 71st floor of the Stamford next door gives great views of the city, and there's a happy hour between 3-9pm.Had to check out at 1pm, but flight wasn't until midnight, so we got access to the courtesy lounge in the hotel. Lounge contains a number of comfortable chairs/couches, plasma screen TV, free coffee/tea, and a bathroom/shower with lots of towels should you need to freshen up.Pre-booked taxi to take us to Changi airport with the concierge, but didn't really need to as there were plenty of taxis dropping off/picking up at the hotel.Overall probably the best hotel we've stayed in in Singapore, highly recommended.  
<Date>Feb 18, 2007

<Author>Finlo
<Content>Good central location, otherwise OK The best feature of this hotel is its location - right on top of City Hall MRT you're well situated for the waterfront area round Raffles Quay and five minutes on the train from Orchard Road. The shopping centre under the hotel has a reasonable range of shops, with a supermarket and food court in the basement.Other good points:A balcony from which to take in the views.Poolside buffet breakfast at the Alligator Pear restaurant, not a fabulous range of food but nice way to start the day.Good standards of cleanliness and nice wet-room style shower (South Tower room).Pools - I didn't use them, but there are two good size pools open early until 10pm, one 1.2m deep, the other 1.2-2m deep. No life guard though if you're with kids.Room service menu offers choices from several of the restaurants in the complex, and generally gets delivered when they say it will.Reasonable range of toiletries provided, plus toothbrushes, nail files, cotton buds, cotton wool balls. Ironing board and iron provided in room, not a lot of coat hangers (I had enough for a four night stay) but at least they provide a couple of padded ones.Downsides (possibly coloured by the fact I normally stay at the Four Seasons in Singapore, so that's my reference):Lighting - even will all the lights on, you'd be pressed to have enough to really work by in the evenings. The nightlight feature on the room console activates the main bathroom light, which then doesn't turn off if you turn the nightlight off. Persistant smell of cooking in the corridors.The balcony is a nice touch, but in my room the wind fair howled through at times (engineering came and replaced the gasket), and it means you do get quite a bit of traffic noise.Room service - some of the local dishes were good (mee goreng or wonton soup for example), but worst hotel burger I've ever had. I complained when they picked up the tray, but had to ask for it to be waived from the bill at checkout. Having asked for olive oil and balsamic on the side for a salad was bemused to get a cup full of malt vinegar. Good job I'd ordered some chips as well!Size - not the rooms, which are pretty good, but overall size. You don't get the personal service that you'd have at smaller 5* hotels.Mini bar - red wine in the fridge? And crummy odd-brand mixers. Schweppes tonic or nothing I say!Getting there and around:From Changi - (on a sunday night) about 25 minutes, just under 20 SGD .City Hall - Orchard on MRT is around 1 SGD if paying with an Ezilink card.Pricing - remember that on checkout you will see additional tax and service charges added to the room rate.

<Author>destinycalls
<Content>Loved Raffles Having read reviews submitted to TripAdvisor we specified the South Tower.The hotel was fabulous. The staff were extremely helpful. We had a room on the 23rd floor. She took the charge off the bill immediately.The lifts were very efficient -we never had to wait more than a few seconds. The hotel is very near to both restaurants and shops.
